            <a href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian" title="Afro-Ecuadorian">
             Afro-Ecuadorian
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            7%
            <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">
             Amerindian
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            6.1%
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">

            </a>

           <li>
            0.4% others
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>

      <p>
       <b>
        Ecuador
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="'w' in 'wind'">
            w
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Ecuador.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/89/En-us-Ecuador.ogg" title="En-us-Ecuador.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          EK
         </span>
         -wə-dor
        </i>
       </a>
       ,
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ekwaˈðor]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">
        Quechua
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="qu">
         Ikwadur
        </span>
       </i>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Ecuador
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         República del Ecuador
        </span>
       </i>
       , which literally translates as "Republic of the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        Equator
       </a>
       ";
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">
        Quechua
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="qu">
         Ikwadur Ripuwlika
        </span>
       </i>
       ), is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representative_democratic" title="Representative democratic">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       republic in northwestern
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       on the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       on the east and south, and the Pacific Ocean to the west. Ecuador also includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">
        Galápagos Islands
       </a>
       in the Pacific, about 1,000 kilometres (620 mi) west of the mainland. The capital city is
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       , while the largest city is
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       What is now Ecuador was home to a variety of
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">
        Amerindian
       </a>
       groups that were gradually incorporated into the
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Inca Empire
       </a>
       during the 15th century. The territory was
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        colonized by Spain
       </a>
       during the 16th century, achieving independence in 1820 as part of
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
        Gran Colombia
       </a>
       , from which it emerged as its own sovereign state in 1830. The legacy of both empires is reflected in Ecuador's ethnically diverse population, with most of its 16.4 million people being
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mestizos" title="Mestizos">
        mestizos
       </a>
       , followed by large minorities of European,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_people_of_Ecuador" title="Indigenous people of Ecuador">
        Amerindian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian" title="Afro-Ecuadorian">
        African
       </a>
       descendants.
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       is the official language and is spoken by a majority of the population, though 13 Amerindian languages are also recognized, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quichua_language" title="Quichua language">
        Quichua
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Shuar_language" title="Shuar language">
        Shuar
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador is a middle-income country, with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_economy" title="Developing economy">
        developing economy
       </a>
       that is highly dependent on commodities, namely petroleum and agricultural products. It is governed as a democratic
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       republic. One of 17
       <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">
        megadiverse countries
       </a>
       in the world,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservation_International_Site_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Conservation_International_Site-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ecuador hosts many
       <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">
        endemic
       </a>
       plants and animals, such as those of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">
        Galápagos Islands
       </a>
       . In recognition of its unique ecological heritage, the new constitution of 2008 is the first in the world to recognize legally enforceable
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rights_of_Nature" title="Rights of Nature">
        Rights of Nature
       </a>
       , or ecosystem rights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">
         <a href="#History">
          <span class="tocnumber">

          <span class="toctext">
           History
          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2">
           <a href="#Pre-Inca_era">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             1.1
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Pre-Inca era
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">
           <a href="#Inca_era">
            <span class="tocnumber">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ecuador" title="History of Ecuador">
        History of Ecuador
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">
        Indigenous peoples in Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Inca_era">
        Pre-Inca era
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Various peoples had settled in the area of the future Ecuador before the arrival of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incas" title="Incas">
        Incas
       </a>
       . The archeological evidence suggests that the
       <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">
        Paleo-Indians
       </a>
       ' first dispersal into the Americas occurred near the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">
        last glacial period
       </a>
       , around 16,500–13,000 years ago. The first Indians who reached Ecuador may have journeyed by land from North and Central America or by boat down the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       coastline. Much later migrations to Ecuador may have come via the Amazon tributaries, others descended from northern
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , and others ascended from the southern part of South America through the Andes. They developed different languages while emerging as unique ethnic groups.
      </p>
      <p>
       Even though their languages were unrelated, these groups developed similar groups of cultures, each based in different environments. The people of the coast developed a fishing, hunting, and gathering culture; the people of the highland Andes developed a sedentary agricultural way of life; and the people of the Amazon basin developed a nomadic hunting-and-gathering mode of existence.
      </p>
      <p>
       Over time these groups began to interact and intermingle with each other so that groups of families in one area became one community or tribe, with a similar language and culture. Many civilizations arose in Ecuador, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valdivia_Culture" title="Valdivia Culture">
        Valdivia Culture
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machalilla_Culture" title="Machalilla Culture">
        Machalilla Culture
       </a>
       on the coast, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quitus" title="Quitus">
        Quitus
       </a>
       (near present-day Quito), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ari" title="Cañari">
        Cañari
       </a>
       (near present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">
        Cuenca
       </a>
       ). Each civilization developed its own distinctive architecture, pottery, and religious interests.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the highland Andes mountains, where life was more sedentary, groups of tribes cooperated and formed villages; thus the first nations based on agricultural resources and the domestication of animals formed. Eventually, through wars and marriage alliances of their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leader" title="Leader">
        leaders
       </a>
       , a group of nations formed confederations. One region consolidated under a confederation called the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shyris&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shyris (page does not exist)">
        Shyris
       </a>
       , which exercised organized trading and bartering between the different regions. Its political and military power came under the rule of the Duchicela blood-line.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Inca_era">
        Inca era
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       When the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incas" title="Incas">
        Incas
       </a>
       arrived, they found that these confederations were so developed that it took the Incas two generations of rulers –
       <a href="/wiki/Topa_Inca_Yupanqui" title="Topa Inca Yupanqui">
        Topa Inca Yupanqui
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Huayna_Capac" title="Huayna Capac">
        Huayna Capac
       </a>
       – to absorb them into the
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Inca Empire
       </a>
       . The native confederations that gave them the most problems were deported to distant areas of Peru, Bolivia, and north Argentina. Similarly, a number of loyal Inca subjects from Peru and Bolivia were brought to Ecuador to prevent rebellion. Thus, the region of highland Ecuador became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Inca Empire
       </a>
       in 1463 sharing the same language.
      </p>
      <p>
       In contrast, when the Incas made incursions into coastal Ecuador and the eastern Amazon jungles of Ecuador, they found both the environment and indigenous people more hostile. Moreover, when the Incas tried to subdue them, these indigenous people withdrew to the interior and resorted to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerrilla" title="Guerrilla">
        guerrilla
       </a>
       tactics. As a result, Inca expansion into the Amazon basin and the Pacific coast of Ecuador was hampered. The indigenous people of the Amazon jungle and coastal Ecuador remained relatively autonomous until the Spanish soldiers and missionaries arrived in force. The Amazonian people and the
       <a href="/wiki/Chachi_people" title="Chachi people">
        Cayapas
       </a>
       of Coastal Ecuador were the only groups to resist Inca and Spanish domination, maintaining their language and culture well into the 21st century.
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the arrival of the Spaniards, the Inca Empire was involved in a
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Civil_War" title="Inca Civil War">
        civil war
       </a>
       . The untimely death of both the heir Ninan Cuchi and the Emperor Huayna Capac, from a European disease that spread into Ecuador, created a power vacuum between two factions. The northern faction headed by Atahualpa claims that Huayna Capac gave a verbal decree before his death about how the empire should be divided. He gave the territories pertaining to present-day Ecuador and northern Peru to his favorite son Atahualpa, who was to rule from Quito; and he gave the rest to
       <a href="/wiki/Hu%C3%A1scar" title="Huáscar">
        Huáscar
       </a>
       , who was to rule from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">
        Cuzco
       </a>
       . He willed that his heart be buried in Quito, his favorite city, and the rest of his body be buried with his ancestors in Cuzco.
      </p>
      <p>
       Huáscar did not recognize his father's will, since it did not follow Inca traditions of naming an Inca through the priests. Huáscar ordered Atahualpa to attend their father's burial in Cuzco and pay homage to him as the new Inca ruler. Atahualpa, with a large number of his father's veteran soldiers, decided to ignore Huáscar, and a civil war ensued. A number of bloody battles took place until finally Huáscar was captured. Atahualpa marched south to Cuzco and massacred the royal family associated with his brother.
      </p>
      <p>
       A small band of Spaniards headed by Francisco Pizarro landed in Tumbez and marched over the Andes Mountains until they reached Cajamarca, where the new Inca Atahualpa was to hold an interview with them. Valverde, the priest, tried to convince Atahualpa that he should join the Catholic Church and declare himself a vassal of Spain. This infuriated Atahualpa so much that he threw the Bible to the ground. At this point the enraged Spaniards, with orders from Valverde, attacked and massacred unarmed escorts of the Inca and captured Atahualpa.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pizarro" title="Pizarro">
        Pizarro
       </a>
       promised to release Atahualpa if he made good his promise of filling a room full of gold. But, after a mock trial, the Spaniards executed Atahualpa by strangulation.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_rule">
        Spanish rule
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       New infectious diseases, endemic to the Europeans, caused high fatalities among the Amerindian population during the first decades of Spanish rule, as they had no
       <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">
        immunity
       </a>
       . At the same time, the natives were forced into the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
         encomienda
        </a>
       </i>
       labor system for the Spanish. In 1563,
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       became the seat of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Audience_of_Quito" title="Royal Audience of Quito">
        real audiencia
       </a>
       (administrative district) of Spain and part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">
        Viceroyalty of Peru
       </a>
       and later the
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">
        Viceroyalty of New Granada
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       After nearly 300 years of Spanish rule, Quito was still a small city numbering 10,000 inhabitants. On August 10, 1809, the city's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">
         criollos
        </a>
       </i>
       called for independence from Spain (first among the peoples of Latin America). They were led by Juan Pío Montúfar, Quiroga, Salinas, and Bishop Cuero y Caicedo. Quito's nickname, "
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luz_de_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Luz de América">
         Luz de América
        </a>
       </i>
       " ("Light of America"), is based on its leading role in trying to secure an independent, local government. Although the new government lasted no more than two months, it had important repercussions and was an inspiration for the independence movement of the rest of Spanish America.
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:35px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="1148" data-file-width="1720" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/120px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/180px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/240px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Ingapirca" title="Ingapirca">
            Ingapirca
           </a>
           ruins northeast of Cañar canton,
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province,_Ecuador" title="Cañar Province, Ecuador">
            Cañar Province
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:36px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="2605" data-file-width="4001" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/120px-Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/180px-Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/240px-Luis_Montero_-_The_Funerals_of_Inca_Atahualpa_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           One of the main events in the conquest of the Incan Empire was the death of
           <a href="/wiki/Atahualpa" title="Atahualpa">
            Atahualpa
           </a>
           , the last
           <a href="/wiki/Sapa_Inca" title="Sapa Inca">
            Sapa Inca
           </a>
           on August 29, 1533
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:30px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg/120px-Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg/180px-Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg/240px-Quito-San_Diego-01.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Spanish Historical Center in
           <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
            Quito
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:26px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="1625" data-file-width="2000" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg/120px-Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg/180px-Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg/240px-Pizarroshipbuilding.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shipwright" title="Shipwright">
            Shipwrights
           </a>
           from Francisco de Orellana's expedition building a small
           <a href="/wiki/Brigantine" title="Brigantine">
            brigantine
           </a>
           , the
           <i>
            San Pedro
           </i>
           .
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">
        Independence
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_War_of_Independence" title="Ecuadorian War of Independence">
        Ecuadorian War of Independence
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AJSucre.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="315" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/AJSucre.jpg/170px-AJSucre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/AJSucre.jpg/255px-AJSucre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/68/AJSucre.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AJSucre.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
          Antonio José de Sucre
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On October 9, 1820,
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       became the first city in Ecuador to gain its independence from Spain. The people were very happy about the independence and celebrated, which is now Ecuador's independence day, officially on May 24, 1822. The rest of Ecuador gained its independence after
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       defeated the Spanish Royalist forces at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pichincha" title="Battle of Pichincha">
        Battle of Pichincha
       </a>
       , near
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       . Following the battle, Ecuador joined
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Simón Bolívar
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Gran_Colombia" title="Republic of Gran Colombia">
        Republic of Gran Colombia
       </a>
       , also including modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       . In 1830 Ecuador separated from Gran Colombia and became an independent republic.
      </p>
      <p>
       The 19th century was marked by instability for Ecuador with a rapid succession of rulers. The first president of Ecuador was the Venezuelan-born
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Flores" title="Juan José Flores">
        Juan José Flores
       </a>
       , who was ultimately deposed, followed by several authoritarian leaders, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Rocafuerte" title="Vicente Rocafuerte">
        Vicente Rocafuerte
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo" title="José Joaquín de Olmedo">
        José Joaquín de Olmedo
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Urbina" title="José María Urbina">
        José María Urbina
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Noboa" title="Diego Noboa">
        Diego Noboa
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Jos%C3%A9_de_Arteta" title="Pedro José de Arteta">
        Pedro José de Arteta
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Asc%C3%A1subi" title="Manuel de Ascásubi">
        Manuel de Ascásubi
       </a>
       ; and Flores's own son,
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Flores_Jij%C3%B3n" title="Antonio Flores Jijón">
        Antonio Flores Jijón
       </a>
       , among others. The conservative
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garcia_Moreno" title="Gabriel Garcia Moreno">
        Gabriel Garcia Moreno
       </a>
       unified the country in the 1860s with the support of the Roman Catholic Church. In the late 19th century, world demand for
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       tied the economy to commodity exports and led to migrations from the highlands to the agricultural frontier on the coast.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">
        abolished
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Latin_America" title="Slavery in Latin America">
        slavery
       </a>
       and freed its black slaves in 1851.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Liberal_Revolution">
        Liberal Revolution
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="506" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/220px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/330px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/440px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Antique
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dugout_(boat)" title="Dugout (boat)">
          dug out canoes
         </a>
         in the courtyard of the Old Military Hospital in the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historic_Center_of_Quito" title="Historic Center of Quito">
          Historic Center of Quito
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1895" title="Liberal Revolution of 1895">
        Liberal Revolution of 1895
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Liberal Revolution of 1895 under
       <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">
        Eloy Alfaro
       </a>
       reduced the power of the clergy and the conservative land owners. This liberal wing retained power until the military "Julian Revolution" of 1925. The 1930s and 1940s were marked by instability and emergence of populist politicians, such as five-time President
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_Ibarra" title="José María Velasco Ibarra">
        José María Velasco Ibarra
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_claimed_territories_since_1830">
        Loss of claimed territories since 1830
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ecuadorian%E2%80%93Peruvian_territorial_dispute" title="History of the Ecuadorian–Peruvian territorial dispute">
        History of the Ecuadorian–Peruvian territorial dispute
       </a>
      </div>
      <div aria-labelledby="The_Ecuadorian–Peruvian_territorial_dispute" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">

            The Ecuadorian–Peruvian territorial dispute
           </span>
          </div>
         </th>
        </tr>
        <tr>
