      </div>
      <h4>
       <span id="President_Juan_Jos.C3.A9_Flores_de_jure_territorial_claims">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="President_Juan_José_Flores_de_jure_territorial_claims">
        President Juan José Flores de jure territorial claims
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Since Ecuador's separation from Colombia in May 13, 1830, its first President, General
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Flores" title="Juan José Flores">
        Juan José Flores
       </a>
       , laid claim to the territory that was called the Real Audiencia of Quito, also referred to as the Presidencia of Quito. He supported his claims with Spanish Royal decrees or
       <i>
        Real Cedulas
       </i>
       , that delineated the borders of Spain's former overseas colonies. In the case of Ecuador, Flores-based Ecuador's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
         de jure
        </a>
       </i>
       claims on the following cedulas - Real Cedula of 1563, 1739, and 1740; with modifications in the Amazon Basin and Andes Mountains that were introduced through the Treaty of Guayaquil (1829) which Peru reluctantly signed, after the overwhelmingly outnumbered Gran Colombian force led by
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       defeated President and General La Mar's Peruvian invasion force in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarqui" title="Battle of Tarqui">
        Battle of Tarqui
       </a>
       . In addition, Ecuador's eastern border with the Portuguese colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       in the Amazon Basin was modified before the wars of Independence by the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Treaty_of_San_Ildefonso" title="First Treaty of San Ildefonso">
        First Treaty of San Ildefonso
       </a>
       (1777) between the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese Empire
       </a>
       . Moreover, to add legitimacy to his claims, on February 16, 1840, Flores signed a treaty with Spain, whereby Flores convinced Spain to officially recognize Ecuadorian independence and its sole rights to colonial titles over Spain's former colonial territory known anciently to Spain as the Kingdom and Presidency of Quito.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador during its long and turbulent history has lost most of its contested territories to each of its more powerful neighbors, such as Colombia in 1832 and 1916, Brazil in 1904 through a series of peaceful treaties, and Peru after a short war in which the Protocol of Rio de Janeiro was signed in 1942.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_for_independence">
        Struggle for independence
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       During the struggle for independence, before Peru or Ecuador became independent nations, a few areas of the former Vice Royalty of New Granada - Guayaquil, Tumbez, and Jaén - declared themselves independent from Spain. A few months later, a part of the Peruvian liberation army of San Martin decided to occupy the independent cities of Tumbez and Jaén with the intention of using these towns as springboards to occupy the independent city of Guayaquil and then to liberate the rest of the Audiencia de Quito (Ecuador). It was common knowledge among the top officers of the liberation army from the south that their leader
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">
        San Martin
       </a>
       wished to liberate present-day Ecuador and add it to the future republic of Peru, since it had been part of the Inca Empire before the Spaniards conquered it.
      </p>
      <p>
       However,
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Bolívar
       </a>
       's intention was to form a new republic known as the Gran Colombia, out of the liberated Spanish territory of New Granada which consisted of Colombia, Venezuela, and Ecuador. San Martin's plans were thwarted when
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Bolívar
       </a>
       , with the help of Marshal Antonio José de Sucre and the Gran Colombian liberation force, descended from the Andes mountains and occupied Guayaquil; they also annexed the newly liberated Audiencia de Quito to the Republic of
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
        Gran Colombia
       </a>
       . This happened a few days before San Martin's Peruvian forces could arrive and occupy Guayaquil, with the intention of annexing Guayaquil to the rest of Audiencia of Quito (Ecuador) and to the future republic of Peru. Historic documents repeatedly stated that San Martin told Bolivar he came to Guayaquil to liberate the land of the Incas from Spain. Bolivar countered by sending a message from Guayaquil welcoming San Martin and his troops to Colombian soil.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Peruvian_occupation_of_Ja.C3.A9n.2C_Tumbes.2C_and_Guayaquil">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Peruvian_occupation_of_Jaén,_Tumbes,_and_Guayaquil">
        Peruvian occupation of Jaén, Tumbes, and Guayaquil
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In the south, Ecuador had
       <i>
        de jure
       </i>
       claims to a small piece of land beside the Pacific Ocean known as
       <a href="/wiki/Tumbes_Region" title="Tumbes Region">
        Tumbes
       </a>
       which lay between the
       <a href="/wiki/Zarumilla_River" title="Zarumilla River">
        Zarumilla
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tumbes_River" title="Tumbes River">
        Tumbes
       </a>
       rivers. In Ecuador's southern Andes Mountain region where the Marañon cuts across, Ecuador had
       <i>
        de jure
       </i>
       claims to an area it called
       <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%A9n,_Peru" title="Jaén, Peru">
        Jaén de Bracamoros
       </a>
       . These areas were included as part of the territory of Gran Colombia by Bolivar in December 17, 1819, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Angostura" title="Congress of Angostura">
        Congress of Angostura
       </a>
       when the Republic of Gran Colombia was created. Tumbes declared itself independent from Spain on January 17, 1821, and Jaen de Bracamoros on June 17, 1821, without any outside help from revolutionary armies. However, that same year, 1821, Peruvian forces participating in the Trujillo revolution occupied both Jaen and Tumbes. Some Peruvian generals, without any legal titles backing them up and with Ecuador still federated with the Gran Colombia, had the desire to annex Ecuador to the Republic of Peru at the expense of the Gran Colombia, feeling that Ecuador was once part of the Inca Empire.
      </p>
      <p>
       On July 28, 1821, Peruvian independence was proclaimed in Lima by the Liberator San Martin and Tumbes and Jaen which were included as part of the revolution of Trujillo by the Peruvian occupying force, had the whole region swear allegiance to the new Peruvian flag and incorporated itself into Peru, even though Peru was not completely liberated from Spain. After Peru was completely liberated from Spain by the patriot armies led by Bolivar and Antonio Jose de Sucre at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ayacucho" title="Battle of Ayacucho">
        Battle of Ayacucho
       </a>
       dated December 9, 1824, there was a strong desire by some Peruvians to resurrect the
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Inca Empire
       </a>
       and to include Bolivia and Ecuador. One of these Peruvian Generals was the Ecuadorian-born
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_La_Mar" title="José de La Mar">
        José de La Mar
       </a>
       , who became one of Peru's presidents after Bolivar resigned as dictator of Peru and returned to Colombia. Gran Colombia had always protested Peru for the return of Jaen and Tumbes for almost a decade, then finally Bolivar after long and futile discussion over the return of Jaen, Tumbes, and part of Mainas, declared war. President and General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_La_Mar" title="José de La Mar">
        José de La Mar
       </a>
       , who was born in Ecuador, believing his opportunity had come to annex the District of Ecuador to Peru, personally, with a Peruvian force, invaded and occupied Guayaquil and a few cities in the Loja region of southern Ecuador on November 28, 1828.
      </p>
      <p>
       The war ended when a triumphant heavily outnumbered southern Gran Colombian army at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarqui" title="Battle of Tarqui">
        Battle of Tarqui
       </a>
       dated February 27, 1829, led by
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       , defeated the Peruvian invasion force led by President La Mar. This defeat led to the signing of the Treaty of Guayaquil dated September 22, 1829, whereby Peru and its Congress recognized Gran Colombian rights over Tumbes, Jaen, and Maynas. Through protocolized meetings between representatives of Peru and Gran Colombia, the border was set as Tumbes river in the west and in the east the Maranon and Amazon rivers were to be followed toward Brazil as the most natural borders between them. However, what was pending was whether the new border around the Jaen region should follow the Chinchipe river or the Huancabamba river. According to the peace negotiations Peru agreed to return Guayaquil, Tumbez, and Jaén; despite this, Peru returned Guayaquil, but failed to return Tumbes and Jaén, alleging that it was not obligated to follow the agreements, since the Gran Colombia ceased to exist when it divided itself into three different nations - Ecuador, Colombia, and Venezuela.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_dissolution_of_Gran_Colombia">
        The dissolution of Gran Colombia
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2315" data-file-width="2829" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg/220px-Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg/330px-Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg/440px-Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gran_Colombia_map_1824.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
          Gran Colombia
         </a>
         showing all Colombian Land Claims outlined in red
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador1830.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="779" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ecuador1830.png/220px-Ecuador1830.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ecuador1830.png/330px-Ecuador1830.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ecuador1830.png/440px-Ecuador1830.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador1830.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ecuador in 1830
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Central District of the Gran Colombia, known as Cundinamarca or New Granada (modern Colombia) with its capital in Bogota, did not recognize the separation of the Southern District of the Gran Colombia, with its capital in Quito, from the Gran Colombian federation on May 13, 1830. After Ecuador's separation, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Cauca" title="Department of Cauca">
        Department of Cauca
       </a>
       voluntarily decided to unite itself with Ecuador due to instability in the central government of Bogota. President Juan José Flores with the approval of the Ecuadorian congress annexed the Department of Cauca on December 20, 1830, since the government of Cauca had called for union with the District of the South as far back as April 1830. Moreover, the Cauca region throughout its long history had very strong economic and cultural ties with the people of Ecuador. Also, the Cauca region which included such cities as
       <a href="/wiki/Pasto,_Colombia" title="Pasto, Colombia">
        Pasto
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Popay%C3%A1n" title="Popayán">
        Popayán
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Buenaventura,_Valle_del_Cauca" title="Buenaventura, Valle del Cauca">
        Buenaventura
       </a>
       had always been dependent on the Presidencia or Audiencia of Quito.
      </p>
      <p>
       Fruitless negotiations continued between the governments of Bogotá and Quito, where the government of Bogotá did not recognize the separation of Ecuador or that of Cauca from the Gran Colombia until war broke out in May 1832. In five months, New Granada defeated Ecuador due to the fact that the majority of the Ecuadorian Armed Forces were composed of rebellious angry unpaid veterans from Venezuela and Colombia that did not want to fight against their fellow countrymen. Seeing that his officers were rebelling, mutinying, and changing sides, President Flores had no option but to reluctantly make peace with New Granada. The Treaty of Pasto of 1832 was signed by which the Department of Cauca was turned over to New Granada (modern Colombia), the government of Bogotá recognized Ecuador as an independent country and the border was to follow the Ley de División Territorial de la República de Colombia (Law of the Division of Territory of the Gran Colombia) passed on June 25, 1824. This law set the border at the river Carchi and the eastern border that stretched to Brazil at the Caquetá river. Later, Ecuador contended that the Republic of Colombia, while reorganizing its government, unlawfully made its eastern border provisional and that Colombia extended its claims south to the Napo River because it said that the Government of Popayán extended its control all the way to the Napo River.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_for_possession_of_the_Amazon_Basin">
        Struggle for possession of the Amazon Basin
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_America_1879.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="465" height="363" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/South_America_1879.png/220px-South_America_1879.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/South_America_1879.png/330px-South_America_1879.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/South_America_1879.png/440px-South_America_1879.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_America_1879.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         South America (1879): All land claims by Peru, Ecuador, Colombia, Brazil, Argentina, Chile, and Bolivia in 1879
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       When Ecuador seceded from the Gran Colombia, Peru decided not to follow the treaty of Guayaquil of 1829 or the protocoled agreements made. Peru contested Ecuador's claims with the newly discovered
       <i>
        Real Cedula
       </i>
       of 1802, by which Peru claims the King of Spain had transferred these lands from the Viceroyalty of New Granada to the Viceroyalty of Peru. During colonial times this was to halt the ever-expanding Portuguese settlements into Spanish domains, which were left vacant and in disorder after the expulsion of Jesuit missionaries from their bases along the Amazon Basin. Ecuador countered by labeling the Cedula of 1802 an ecclesiastical instrument, which had nothing to do with political borders. Peru began its de facto occupation of disputed Amazonian territories, after it signed a secret 1851 peace treaty in favor of Brazil. This treaty disregarded Spanish rights that were confirmed during colonial times by a Spanish-Portuguese treaty over the Amazon regarding territories held by illegal Portuguese settlers.
      </p>
      <p>
       Peru began occupying the defenseless missionary villages in the Mainas or Maynas region which it began calling Loreto with its capital in
       <a href="/wiki/Iquitos" title="Iquitos">
        Iquitos
       </a>
       . During its negotiations with Brazil, Peru stated that based on the royal cedula of 1802, it claimed Amazonian Basin territories up to Caqueta River in the north and toward the Andes Mountain range, depriving Ecuador and Colombia of all their claims to the Amazon Basin. Colombia protested stating that its claims extended south toward the Napo and Amazon Rivers. Ecuador protested that it claimed the Amazon Basin between the Caqueta river and the Marañon-Amazon river. Peru ignored these protests and created the Department of Loreto in 1853 with its capital in Iquitos which it had recently invaded and systematically began to occupy using the river systems in all the territories claimed by both Colombia and Ecuador. Peru briefly occupied Guayaquil again in 1860, since Peru thought that Ecuador was selling some of the disputed land for development to British bond holders, but returned Guayaquil after a few months. The border dispute was then submitted to Spain for arbitration from 1880 to 1910, but to no avail.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early part of the 20th century Ecuador made an effort to peacefully define its eastern Amazonian borders with its neighbours through negotiation. On May 6, 1904, Ecuador signed the Tobar-Rio Branco Treaty recognizing Brazil's claims to the Amazon in recognition of Ecuador's claim to be an Amazonian country to counter Peru's earlier Treaty with Brazil back in October 23, 1851. Then after a few meetings with the Colombian government's representatives an agreement was reached and the Muñoz Vernaza-Suarez Treaty was signed July 15, 1916, in which Colombian rights to the Putumayo river were recognized as well as Ecuador's rights to the Napo river and the new border was a line that ran midpoint between those two rivers. In this way Ecuador gave up the claims it had to the Amazonian territories between the Caquetá River and Napo River to Colombia, thus cutting itself off from Brazil. Later a brief war erupted between Colombia and Peru, over Peru's claims to the Caquetá region, which ended with the Peru reluctantly signing the Salomon-Lozano Treaty on March 24, 1922. Ecuador protested this secret treaty, since Colombia gave away Ecuadorian claimed land to Peru that Ecuador had given to Colombia in 1916.
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 21, 1924 the Ponce-Castro Oyanguren Protocol was signed between Ecuador and Peru where both agreed to hold direct negotiations and to resolve the dispute in an equitable manner and to submit the differing points of the dispute to the United States for arbitration. Negotiations between the Ecuadorian and Peruvian representatives began in Washington on September 30, 1935. These negotiations were long and tiresome. Both sides logically presented their cases, but no one seemed to give up their claims. Then on February 6, 1937, Ecuador presented a transactional line which Peru rejected the next day. The negotiations turned into intense arguments during the next 7 months and finally on September 29, 1937 the Peruvian representatives decided to break off the negotiations without submitting the dispute to arbitration because the direct negotiations were going nowhere.
      </p>
      <p>
       Four years later in 1941, amid fast-growing tensions within disputed territories around the Zarumilla River, war broke out with Peru. Peru claimed that Ecuador's military presence in Peruvian-claimed territory was an invasion; Ecuador, for its part, claimed that Peru had recently invaded Ecuador around the Zarumilla River and that Peru since Ecuador's independence from Spain has systematically occupied Tumbez, Jaen, and most of the disputed territories in the Amazonian Basin between the Putomayo and Marañon Rivers. In July 1941, troops were mobilized in both countries. Peru had an army of 11,681 troops who faced a poorly supplied and inadequately armed Ecuadorian force of 2,300, of which only 1,300 were deployed in the southern provinces. Hostilities erupted on July 5, 1941, when Peruvian forces crossed the Zarumilla river at several locations, testing the strength and resolve of the Ecuadorian border troops. Finally, on July 23, 1941, the Peruvians launched a major invasion, crossing the Zarumilla river in force and advancing into the Ecuadorian province of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">
        El Oro
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="731" data-file-width="1000" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png/220px-Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png/330px-Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png/440px-Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador-peru-land-claims-01.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Ecuadorian Land Claims after 1916
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the course of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian%E2%80%93Peruvian_War" title="Ecuadorian–Peruvian War">
        Ecuadorian–Peruvian War
       </a>
       , Peru gained control over part of the disputed territory and some parts of the province of El Oro, and some parts of the
       <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">
        province of Loja
       </a>
       , demanding that the Ecuadorian government give up its territorial claims. The Peruvian Navy blocked the port of
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       , almost cutting all supplies to the Ecuadorian troops. After a few weeks of war and under pressure by the United States and several Latin American nations, all fighting came to a stop. Ecuador and Peru came to an accord formalized in the
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Protocol" title="Rio Protocol">
        Rio Protocol
       </a>
       , signed on January 29, 1942, in favor of hemispheric unity against the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">
        Axis Powers
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       favouring Peru with the territory they occupied at the time the war came to an end.
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1944
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Glorious_May_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Glorious May Revolution (page does not exist)">
        Glorious May Revolution
       </a>
       followed a military-civilian rebellion and a subsequent civic strike which successfully removed Carlos Arroyo del Río as a dictator from Ecuador's government. However, a post-Second World War recession and popular unrest led to a return to populist politics and domestic military interventions in the 1960s, while foreign companies developed oil resources in the Ecuadorian Amazon. In 1972, construction of the Andean pipeline was completed. The pipeline brought oil from the east side of the Andes to the coast, making Ecuador South America's second largest oil exporter. The pipeline in southern Ecuador did nothing to resolve tensions between Ecuador and Peru, however.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relevo-ecu.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="272" data-file-width="557" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Relevo-ecu.JPG/220px-Relevo-ecu.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Relevo-ecu.JPG/330px-Relevo-ecu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Relevo-ecu.JPG/440px-Relevo-ecu.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relevo-ecu.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ecuadorian troops during the
         <a href="/wiki/Cenepa_War" title="Cenepa War">
          Cenepa War
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mirage_F.1JA.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1700" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mirage_F.1JA.JPG/220px-Mirage_F.1JA.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mirage_F.1JA.JPG/330px-Mirage_F.1JA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mirage_F.1JA.JPG/440px-Mirage_F.1JA.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mirage_F.1JA.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_F1" title="Dassault Mirage F1">
          Mirage F.1JA
         </a>
         (FAE-806) was one aircraft involved in the claimed shooting down of two Peruvian
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-22" title="Sukhoi Su-22">
          Sukhoi Su-22
         </a>
         on February 10, 1995.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Protocol" title="Rio Protocol">
        Rio Protocol
       </a>
       failed to precisely resolve the border along a little river in the remote
       <i>
        Cordillera del Cóndor
       </i>
       region in southern Ecuador. This caused a long-simmering dispute between Ecuador and Peru, which ultimately led to fighting between the two countries; first a border skirmish in January–February 1981 known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paquisha_Incident" title="Paquisha Incident">
        Paquisha Incident
       </a>
       , and ultimately full-scale warfare in January 1995 where the Ecuadorian military shot down Peruvian aircraft and helicopters and Peruvian infantry marched into southern Ecuador. Each country blamed the other for the onset of hostilities, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Cenepa_War" title="Cenepa War">
        Cenepa War
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Sixto_Dur%C3%A1n_Ball%C3%A9n" title="Sixto Durán Ballén">
        Sixto Durán Ballén
       </a>
       , the Ecuadorian president, famously declared that he would not give up a single centimeter of Ecuador. Popular sentiment in Ecuador became strongly
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
        nationalistic
       </a>
       against Peru: graffiti could be seen on the walls of Quito referring to Peru as the "
       <i>
        Cain de Latinoamérica
       </i>
       ", a reference to the murder of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abel" title="Abel">
        Abel
       </a>
       by his brother
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cain" title="Cain">
        Cain
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">
        Book of Genesis
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador and Peru signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Brasilia_Presidential_Act" title="Brasilia Presidential Act">
        Brasilia Presidential Act
       </a>
       peace agreement on October 26, 1998, which ended hostilities, and effectively put an end to the Western Hemisphere's longest running territorial dispute.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ucdp.uu.se_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ucdp.uu.se-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Guarantors of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Protocol" title="Rio Protocol">
        Rio Protocol
       </a>
       (Argentina, Brazil, Chile, and the United States of America) ruled that the border of the undelineated zone was to be set at the line of the
       <i>
        Cordillera del Cóndor
       </i>
       . While Ecuador had to give up its decades-old territorial claims to the eastern slopes of the Cordillera, as well as to the entire western area of Cenepa headwaters, Peru was compelled to give to Ecuador, in perpetual lease but without sovereignty, 1 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       of its territory, in the area where the Ecuadorian base of Tiwinza – focal point of the war – had been located within Peruvian soil and which the Ecuadorian Army held during the conflict. The final border demarcation came into effect on May 13, 1999 and the multi-national MOMEP (Military Observer Mission for Ecuador and Peru) troop deployment withdrew on June 17, 1999.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ucdp.uu.se_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ucdp.uu.se-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Military_governments_.281972.E2.80.9379.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military_governments_(1972–79)">
        Military governments (1972–79)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1972, a "revolutionary and nationalist" military
       <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">
        junta
       </a>
       overthrew the government of Velasco Ibarra. The
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       was led by General
       <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(politician)" title="Guillermo Rodríguez (politician)">
        Guillermo Rodríguez
       </a>
       and executed by navy commander Jorge Queirolo G. The new president exiled José María Velasco to
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       . He remained in power until 1976, when he was removed by another military government. That military junta was led by Admiral
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Poveda" title="Alfredo Poveda">
        Alfredo Poveda
       </a>
       , who was declared chairman of the Supreme Council. The Supreme Council included two other members: General Guillermo Durán Arcentales and General Luis Leoro Franco. The civil society more and more insistently called for democratic elections. Colonel
       <a href="/wiki/Richelieu_Levoyer" title="Richelieu Levoyer">
        Richelieu Levoyer
       </a>
       , Government Minister, proposed and implemented a Plan to return to the constitutional system through universal elections. This plan enabled the new democratically elected president to assume the duties of the executive office.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_democracy">
        Return to democracy
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Elections were held on April 29, 1979, under a new constitution.
       <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Rold%C3%B3s_Aguilera" title="Jaime Roldós Aguilera">
        Jaime Roldós Aguilera
       </a>
       was elected president, garnering over one million votes, the most in Ecuadorian history. He took office on August 10, as the first constitutionally elected president after nearly a decade of civilian and military dictatorships. In 1980, he founded the
       <i>
        Partido Pueblo, Cambio y Democracia
       </i>
       (People, Change, and Democracy Party) after withdrawing from the
       <i>
        Concentración de Fuerzas Populares
       </i>
       (Popular Forces Concentration) and governed until May 24, 1981, when he died along with his wife and the minister of defense,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Subia_Martinez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marco Subia Martinez (page does not exist)">
        Marco Subia Martinez
       </a>
       , when his Air Force plane crashed in heavy rain near the Peruvian border. Many people believe that he was assassinated by the CIA,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       given the multiple death threats leveled against him because of his reformist agenda, deaths in automobile crashes of two key witnesses before they could testify during the investigation, and the sometimes contradictory accounts of the incident.
      </p>
      <p>
       Roldos was immediately succeeded by Vice President Osvaldo Hurtado, who was followed in 1984 by
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_Febres_Cordero" title="León Febres Cordero">
        León Febres Cordero
       </a>
       from the Social Christian Party.
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Borja_Cevallos" title="Rodrigo Borja Cevallos">
        Rodrigo Borja Cevallos
       </a>
       of the Democratic Left (Izquierda Democrática, or ID) party won the presidency in 1988, running in the runoff election against
       <a href="/wiki/Abdal%C3%A1_Bucaram" title="Abdalá Bucaram">
        Abdalá Bucaram
       </a>
       (brother in law of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaime_Roldos" title="Jaime Roldos">
        Jaime Roldos
       </a>
       and founder of the Ecuadorian Roldosist Party). His government was committed to improving human rights protection and carried out some reforms, notably an opening of Ecuador to foreign trade. The Borja government concluded an accord leading to the disbanding of the small terrorist group, "
       <a href="/wiki/%C2%A1Alfaro_Vive,_Carajo!" title="¡Alfaro Vive, Carajo!">
        ¡Alfaro Vive, Carajo!
       </a>
       " ("Alfaro Lives, Dammit!"), named after
       <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">
        Eloy Alfaro
       </a>
       . However, continuing economic problems undermined the popularity of the ID, and opposition parties gained control of Congress in 1999.
      </p>
      <p>
       The emergence of the Amerindian population as an active constituency has added to the democratic volatility of the country in recent years. The population has been motivated by government failures to deliver on promises of land reform, lower unemployment and provision of social services, and historical exploitation by the land-holding elite. Their movement, along with the continuing destabilizing efforts by both the elite and leftist movements, has led to a deterioration of the executive office. The populace and the other branches of government give the president very little political capital, as illustrated by the most recent removal of President
       <a href="/wiki/Lucio_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Lucio Gutiérrez">
        Lucio Gutiérrez
       </a>
       from office by Congress in April 2005. Vice President
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Palacio" title="Alfredo Palacio">
        Alfredo Palacio
       </a>
       took his place and remained in office until the presidential
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_general_election,_2006" title="Ecuadorian general election, 2006">
        election of 2006
       </a>
       , in which
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">
        Rafael Correa
       </a>
       gained the presidency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rory_Carroll,_Latin_America_correspondent_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rory_Carroll,_Latin_America_correspondent-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2008, president Correa declared Ecuador's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_debt" title="National debt">
        national debt
       </a>
       illegitimate, based on the argument that it was
       <a href="/wiki/Odious_debt" title="Odious debt">
        odious debt
       </a>
       contracted by corrupt and despotic prior regimes. He announced that the country would default on over $3 billion worth of bonds; he then pledged to fight creditors in
       <a href="/wiki/International_court" title="International court">
        international courts
       </a>
       and succeeded in reducing the price of outstanding bonds by more than 60%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TRN2009Win_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TRN2009Win-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He brought Ecuador into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">
        Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas
       </a>
       in June 2009. To date, Correa's administration has succeeded in reducing the high levels of poverty and unemployment in Ecuador.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Romero_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Romero-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_Popular_E-mail_Newsletter_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Most_Popular_E-mail_Newsletter-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ecuador" title="Politics of Ecuador">
        Politics of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Correarafael15012007.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="724" data-file-width="641" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Correarafael15012007.jpg/170px-Correarafael15012007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Correarafael15012007.jpg/255px-Correarafael15012007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Correarafael15012007.jpg/340px-Correarafael15012007.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Correarafael15012007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The former President Rafael Correa assumed office on January 15, 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Ecuadorian State consists of five branches of government: the
       <i>
        Executive Branch
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Legislative Branch
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Judicial Branch
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Electoral Branch
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Transparency and Social Control.
       </i>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador is governed by a democratically elected President, for a four-year term. The current president of Ecuador,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenin_Moreno" title="Lenin Moreno">
        Lenin Moreno
       </a>
       , exercises his power from the presidential
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Carondelet" title="Palacio de Carondelet">
        Palacio de Carondelet
       </a>
       in Quito. The
       <a href="/wiki/2008_Constitution_of_Ecuador" title="2008 Constitution of Ecuador">
        current constitution
       </a>
       was written by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Constituent_Assembly" title="Ecuadorian Constituent Assembly">
        Ecuadorian Constituent Assembly
       </a>
       elected in 2007, and was approved by referendum in 2008. Since 1936, voting is compulsory for all literate persons aged 18–65, optional for all other citizens.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The executive branch includes 23 ministries. Provincial governors and councilors (mayors, aldermen, and parish boards) are directly elected. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Ecuador" title="National Assembly of Ecuador">
        National Assembly of Ecuador
       </a>
       meets throughout the year except for recesses in July and December. There are thirteen permanent committees. Members of the National Court of Justice are appointed by the National Judicial Council for nine-year terms.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">
        Executive branch
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Ecuador" title="List of heads of state of Ecuador">
        List of heads of state of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG/220px-Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG/330px-Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG/440px-Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carondelet_-_Quito.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Carondelet" title="Palacio de Carondelet">
          Palacio de Carondelet
         </a>
         , the executive branch of the Ecuadorian Government
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
        executive branch
       </a>
       is led by the president, an office currently held by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenin_Moreno" title="Lenin Moreno">
        Lenin Moreno
       </a>
       . He is accompanied by the vice-president, currently
       <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Glas" title="Jorge Glas">
        Jorge Glas
       </a>
       , elected for four years (with the ability to be re-elected only once). As head of state and chief government official, he is responsible for public administration including the appointing of national coordinators, ministers, ministers of State and public servants. The executive branch defines foreign policy, appoints the Chancellor of the Republic, as well as ambassadors and consuls, being the ultimate authority over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Ecuador" title="Military of Ecuador">
        Armed Forces of Ecuador
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Ecuador" title="National Police of Ecuador">
        National Police of Ecuador
       </a>
       , and appointing authorities. The acting president's wife receives the title of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_Ecuador" title="First Lady of Ecuador">
        First Lady of Ecuador
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">
        Legislative branch
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Ecuador)" title="National Assembly (Ecuador)">
        National Assembly (Ecuador)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The legislative branch is embodied by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Ecuador" title="National Assembly of Ecuador">
        National Assembly
       </a>
       , which is headquartered in the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       in the Legislative Palace, and consists of 137 assemblymen, divided into ten committees and elected for a four-year term. Fifteen national constituency elected assembly, two Assembly members elected from each province and one for every 100,000 inhabitants or fraction exceeding 150,000, according to the latest national population census. In addition, statute determines the election of assembly of regions, and metropolitan districts.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">
        Judicial branch
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Ecuador's judiciary has as its main body the Judicial Council, and also includes the National Court of Justice, provincial courts, and lower courts. Legal representation is made by the Judicial Council. The National Court of Justice is composed of 21 judges elected for a term of nine years. Judges are renewed by thirds every three years pursuant to the Judicial Code. These are elected by the Judicial Council on the basis of opposition proceedings and merits. The justice system is buttressed by the independent offices of public prosecutor and the public defender. Auxiliary organs are as follows:
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_notary" title="Civil law notary">
        notaries
       </a>
       , court auctioneers, and court receivers. Also there is a special legal regime for Amerindians.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_branch">
        Electoral branch
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The electoral system functions by authorities which enter only every four years or when
       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Ecuador" title="Elections in Ecuador">
        elections or referendums
       </a>
       occur. Its main functions are to organize, control elections, and punish the infringement of electoral rules. Its main body is the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Electoral_Council_(Ecuador)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Electoral Council (Ecuador) (page does not exist)">
        National Electoral Council
       </a>
       , which is based in the city of Quito, and consists of seven members of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_Ecuador" title="Political parties in Ecuador">
        political parties
       </a>
       most voted, enjoying complete financial and administrative autonomy. This body, along with the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Electoral_Tribunal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Electoral Tribunal (page does not exist)">
        electoral court
       </a>
       , forms the
       <i>
        Electoral Branch
       </i>
       which is one of Ecuador's five
       <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">
        branches of government
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transparency_and_social_control_branch">
        Transparency and social control branch
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Transparency and Social Control consists of the Council of Citizen Participation and Social Control, an
       <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">
        ombudsman
       </a>
       , the Comptroller General of the State, and the superintendents. Branch members hold office for five years. This branch is responsible for promoting transparency and control plans publicly, as well as plans to design mechanisms to combat corruption, as also designate certain authorities, and be the regulatory mechanism of accountability in the country.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
        Human rights
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">
        UN's Human Rights Council
       </a>
       's (HRC) Universal Periodic Review (UPR) has treated the restrictions on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" title="Freedom of expression">
        freedom of expression
       </a>
       and efforts to control
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">
        NGOs
       </a>
       and recommended that Ecuador should stop the criminal sanctions for the expression of opinions, and delay in implementing judicial reforms. Ecuador rejected the recommendation on decriminalization of libel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">
        Human Rights Watch
       </a>
       (HRW) President Correa has intimidated journalists and subjected them to "public denunciation and retaliatory litigation". The sentences to journalists have been years of imprisonment and millions of dollars of compensation, even though defendants have been pardoned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Correa has stated he was only seeking a retraction for slanderous statements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to HRW, Correa's government has weakened the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_of_press" title="Freedom of press">
        freedom of press
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_independence" title="Judicial independence">
        independence of the judicial system
       </a>
       . In Ecuador's current judicial system, judges are selected in a contest of merits, rather than government appointments. However, the process of selection has been criticized as biased and subjective. In particular, the final interview is said to be given "excessive weighing." Judges and prosecutors that have made decisions in favor of Correa in his lawsuits have received permanent posts, while others with better assessment grades have been rejected.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reformahasta2015_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Reformahasta2015-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/220px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/330px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/440px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Adult
         <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_sea_lion" title="Galápagos sea lion">
          Galápagos sea lion
         </a>
         resting on a park bench in
         <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno" title="Puerto Baquerizo Moreno">
          Puerto Baquerizo Moreno
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The laws also forbid articles and media messages that could favor or disfavor some political message or candidate. In the first half of 2012, twenty private TV or radio stations were closed down.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2012 the officials warned the judges that they would be sanctioned and possibly dismissed if they allowed the citizens to appeal to the protection of their constitutional rights against the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       People engaging in public protests against environmental and other issues are prosecuted for "terrorism and sabotage", which may lead to an eight-year prison sentence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_25-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs">
        Foreign affairs
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Ecuador" title="Foreign relations of Ecuador">
        Foreign relations of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador's principal foreign policy objectives have traditionally included defense of its territory from external aggression and support for the objectives of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       and the OAS. Ecuador's membership in the OPEC in the 1970s and 1980s allowed Ecuadorian leaders to exercise somewhat greater foreign policy autonomy. In Antarctica, Ecuador has maintained a peaceful research station for scientific study as a member nation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antarctica_Treaty" title="Antarctica Treaty">
        Antarctica Treaty
       </a>
       . Ecuador has often placed great emphasis on multilateral approaches to international issues. Ecuador is a member of the United Nations (and most of its specialized agencies) and a member of many regional groups, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">
        Rio Group
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Economic_System" title="Latin American Economic System">
        Latin American Economic System
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_American_Energy_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Latin American Energy Organization (page does not exist)">
        Latin American Energy Organization
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Integration_Association" title="Latin American Integration Association">
        Latin American Integration Association
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">
        Bolivarian Alliance for the Peoples of Our America
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" title="Andean Community of Nations">
        Andean Community of Nations
       </a>
       , the Union of South American Nations (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNASUR" title="UNASUR">
        UNASUR
       </a>
       ), and The Bank of the South (Spanish: Banco del Sur or BancoSur).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ecuador" title="Provinces of Ecuador">
        Provinces of Ecuador
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Ecuador" title="Cantons of Ecuador">
        Cantons of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador is divided into 24
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ecuador" title="Provinces of Ecuador">
        provinces
       </a>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         provincias
        </span>
       </i>
       ), each with its own administrative capital:
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="500" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg/220px-Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg/330px-Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg/440px-Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_provinces-numbers.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Ecuador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

         Extent of Ecuador's western
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EEZ" title="EEZ">
          EEZ
         </a>
         in the Pacific
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <p>
       The provinces are divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Ecuador" title="Cantons of Ecuador">
        cantons
       </a>
       and further subdivided into parishes (
       <i>
        parroquias
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_planning_areas">
        Regions and planning areas
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Regionalization, or zoning, is the union of two or more adjoining provinces in order to decentralize the administrative functions of the capital Quito. In Ecuador there are seven regions or zones, each shaped by the following provinces:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Region 1 (42,126 km², or 16,265 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_(province)" title="Esmeraldas (province)">
         Esmeraldas
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carchi" title="Carchi">
         Carchi
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Imbabura_Province" title="Imbabura Province">
         Imbabura
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sucumbios" title="Sucumbios">
         Sucumbios
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a href="/wiki/Ibarra,_Ecuador" title="Ibarra, Ecuador">
         Ibarra
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 2 (43,498 km², or 16,795 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pichincha_(province)" title="Pichincha (province)">
         Pichincha
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napo_(province)" title="Napo (province)">
         Napo
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Orellana_Province" title="Orellana Province">
         Orellana
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a href="/wiki/Tena,_Ecuador" title="Tena, Ecuador">
         Tena
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 3 (44,710 km², or 17,263 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(province)" title="Chimborazo (province)">
         Chimborazo
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tungurahua_(province)" title="Tungurahua (province)">
         Tungurahua
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pastaza_(province)" title="Pastaza (province)">
         Pastaza
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotopaxi_(province)" title="Cotopaxi (province)">
         Cotopaxi
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riobamba,_Ecuador" title="Riobamba, Ecuador">
         Riobamba
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 4 (22,257 km², or 8,594 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a href="/wiki/Manab%C3%AD_Province" title="Manabí Province">
         Manabí
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo_de_los_Tsachilas" title="Santo Domingo de los Tsachilas">
         Santo Domingo de los Tsachilas
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ciudad_Alfaro,_Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ciudad Alfaro, Ecuador (page does not exist)">
         Ciudad Alfaro
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 5 (38,420 km², or 14,834 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">
         Santa Elena
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayas_(province)" title="Guayas (province)">
         Guayas
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Los_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Los Ríos Province">
         Los Ríos
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos" title="Galápagos">
         Galápagos
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Province_(Ecuador)" title="Bolívar Province (Ecuador)">
         Bolívar
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a href="/wiki/Milagro,_Ecuador" title="Milagro, Ecuador">
         Milagro
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 6 (38,237 km², or 14,763 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province,_Ecuador" title="Cañar Province, Ecuador">
         Cañar
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azuay" title="Azuay">
         Azuay
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morona_Santiago" title="Morona Santiago">
         Morona Santiago
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuenca_(Ecuador)" title="Cuenca (Ecuador)">
         Cuenca
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Region 7 (27,571 km², or 10,645 mi
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        ):
        <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">
         El Oro
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">
         Loja
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zamora_Chinchipe" title="Zamora Chinchipe">
         Zamora Chinchipe
        </a>
        . Administrative city:
        <a href="/wiki/Loja,_Ecuador" title="Loja, Ecuador">
         Loja
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       are Metropolitan Districts.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos" title="Galápagos">
        Galápagos
       </a>
       , despite being included within Region 5,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is also under a special unit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Ecuador" title="Military of Ecuador">
        Military of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Superpuma-ecu.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="551" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/220px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/330px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/440px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Superpuma-ecu.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puma_helicopter" title="Puma helicopter">
          Puma helicopter
         </a>
         from the Army's Aviation Branch
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kfir_CE_front.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/220px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/330px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/440px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kfir_CE_front.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">
          Ecuadorian Air Force
         </a>
         (FAE)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Submarino_Shyri.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg/220px-Submarino_Shyri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg/330px-Submarino_Shyri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Submarino_Shyri.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Shyri_(SS-101)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BAE Shyri (SS-101) (page does not exist)">
          BAE Shyri (SS-101)
         </a>
         <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
          (
          <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Shyri_(SS-101)" title="es:BAE Shyri (SS-101)">
           es
          </a>
          )
         </span>
         from the Ecuadorian Navy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Ecuador" title="Military of Ecuador">
        Ecuadorian Armed Forces
       </a>
       (Fuerzas Armadas del Ecuador), consists of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Army" title="Ecuadorian Army">
        Army
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">
        Air Force
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Navy" title="Ecuadorian Navy">
        Navy
       </a>
       and have the stated responsibility for the preservation of the integrity and national sovereignty of the national territory.
      </p>
      <p>
       The military tradition starts in
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">
        Gran Colombia
       </a>
       , where a sizable army was stationed in Ecuador due to border disputes with Peru, which claimed territories under its political control when it was a Spanish vice-royalty. Once Gran Colombia was dissolved after the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Simón Bolívar
       </a>
       in 1830, Ecuador inherited the same border disputes and had the need of creating its own professional military force. So influential was the military in Ecuador in the early republican period that its first decade was under the control of General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_Jose_Flores" title="Juan Jose Flores">
        Juan Jose Flores
       </a>
       , first president of Ecuador of Venezuelan origin. General Jose Ma. Urbina and General Robles are examples of military figures who became presidents of the country in the early republican period.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to the continuous border disputes with Peru, finally settled in the early 2000s, and due to the ongoing problem with the Colombian guerrilla insurgency infiltrating Amazonian provinces, the Ecuadorian Armed Forces has gone through a series of changes. In 2009, the new administration at the Defense Ministry launched a deep restructuring within the forces, increasing spending budget to $1,691,776,803, an increase of 25%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The icons of the Ecuadorian military forces are the Marshall Antonio José de Sucre and General
       <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">
        Eloy Alfaro
       </a>
       . The Military Academy General Eloy Alfaro (c. 1838) graduates the army officers and is located in Quito.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ecuadorian Navy Academy (c. 1837), located in Salinas graduates the navy officers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the Air Academy "Cosme Rennella (c. 1920), also located in Salinas, graduates the air force officers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other training academies for different military specialties are found across the country.
      </p>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_Topography.png" title="Enlarge">
