         </div>
         Ecuador topography
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo,_Ecuador.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg/220px-Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg/330px-Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg/440px-Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo%2C_Ecuador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vicu%C3%B1a_-_Chimborazo,_Ecuador.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Vicu%C3%B1a" title="Vicuña">
          vicuña
         </a>
         , one of two wild South American camelids. In the background the point on the Earth's surface that is farthest from the Earth's center,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(volcano)" title="Chimborazo (volcano)">
          Chimborazo volcano
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
          <a href="#cite_note-35">
           [35]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
          <a href="#cite_note-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador has a total area of 283,561 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (109,484 sq mi), including the
       <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">
        Galápagos Islands
       </a>
       . Of this, 276,841 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (106,889 sq mi) is land and 6,720 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (2,595 sq mi) water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAfactbook_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIAfactbook-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ecuador is bigger than Uruguay, Suriname, Guyana and French Guyana in
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">
        2°N
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">
        5°S
       </a>
       , bounded on the west by the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       , and has 2,337 km (1,452 mi) of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastline" title="Coastline">
        coastline
       </a>
       . It has 2,010 km (1,250 mi) of land boundaries, with
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       in the north 590 km (367 mi) border and Peru in the east and south 1,420 km (882 mi) border. It is the westernmost country that lies on the equator.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The country has four main geographic regions:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         La Costa
        </b>
        , or "the coast": The coastal region consists of the provinces to the West of the Andean range –
        <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_Province" title="Esmeraldas Province">
         Esmeraldas
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">
         Guayas
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Los_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Los Ríos Province">
         Los Ríos
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Manab%C3%AD_Province" title="Manabí Province">
         Manabí
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">
         El Oro
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">
         Santa Elena
        </a>
        . It is the country's most fertile and productive land, and is the seat of the large
        <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">
         banana
        </a>
        exportation plantations of the companies
        <a href="/wiki/Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company">
         Dole
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chiquita" title="Chiquita">
         Chiquita
        </a>
        . This region is also where most of Ecuador's
        <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">
         rice
        </a>
        crop is grown. The truly coastal provinces have active fisheries. The largest coastal city is
        <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
         Guayaquil
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         La Sierra
        </b>
        , or "the highlands": The sierra consists of the Andean and Interandean highland provinces –
        <a href="/wiki/Azuay_Province" title="Azuay Province">
         Azuay
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province" title="Cañar Province">
         Cañar
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Carchi_Province" title="Carchi Province">
         Carchi
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_Province" title="Chimborazo Province">
         Chimborazo
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Imbabura_Province" title="Imbabura Province">
         Imbabura
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">
         Loja
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province" title="Pichincha Province">
         Pichincha
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Tungurahua_Province" title="Tungurahua Province">
         Tungurahua
        </a>
        . This land contains most of Ecuador's volcanoes and all of its snow-capped peaks. Agriculture is focused on the traditional crops of
        <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
         potato
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
         maize
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Quinoa" title="Quinoa">
         quinua
        </a>
        and the population is predominantly Amerindian
        <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">
         Kichua
        </a>
        . The largest Sierran city is
        <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
         Quito
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         La Amazonía
        </b>
        , also known as
        <i>
         El Oriente
        </i>
        , or "the east": The oriente consists of the
        <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
         Amazon jungle
        </a>
        provinces –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morona_Santiago_Province" title="Morona Santiago Province">
         Morona Santiago
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Napo_Province" title="Napo Province">
         Napo
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Orellana_Province" title="Orellana Province">
         Orellana
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_Province" title="Pastaza Province">
         Pastaza
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sucumb%C3%ADos_Province" title="Sucumbíos Province">
         Sucumbíos
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Zamora-Chinchipe_Province" title="Zamora-Chinchipe Province">
         Zamora-Chinchipe
        </a>
        . This region is primarily made up of the huge Amazon national parks and Amerindian untouchable zones, which are vast stretches of land set aside for the Amazon Amerindian tribes to continue living traditionally. It is also the area with the largest reserves of
        <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
         petroleum
        </a>
        in Ecuador, and parts of the upper Amazon here have been extensively exploited by petroleum companies. The population is primarily mixed Amerindian
        <a href="/wiki/Shuar" title="Shuar">
         Shuar
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huaorani" title="Huaorani">
         Huaorani
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">
         Kichua
        </a>
        , although there are numerous tribes in the deep jungle which are little-contacted. The largest city in the Oriente is probably
        <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Loja" title="Nueva Loja">
         Lago Agrio
        </a>
        in Sucumbíos, although
        <a href="/wiki/Macas_(city)" title="Macas (city)">
         Macas
        </a>
        in Morona Santiago runs a close second.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         La Región Insular
        </b>
        is the region comprising the
        <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">
         Galápagos Islands
        </a>
        , some 1,000 kilometres (620 mi) west of the mainland in the Pacific Ocean.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Ecuador's capital is Quito, which is in the province of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province,_Ecuador" title="Pichincha Province, Ecuador">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       in the Sierra region. Its largest city is Guayaquil, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">
        Guayas Province
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">
        Cotopaxi
       </a>
       , which is just south of Quito, features one of the world's highest active volcanoes. The top of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(volcano)" title="Chimborazo (volcano)">
        Mount Chimborazo
       </a>
       (6,268 m, or 20,560 ft, above sea level) is considered to be the most distant point of the Earth's surface from the center of the Earth, given the approximately
       <a href="/wiki/Ellipsoid" title="Ellipsoid">
        ellipsoid
       </a>
       shape of the planet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ecuador" title="Climate of Ecuador">
        Climate of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1465" data-file-width="1900" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ecuador map of
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
          Köppen climate classification
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There is great variety in the climate, largely determined by altitude. It is mild year-round in the mountain valleys, with a
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
        humid subtropical climate
       </a>
       in coastal areas and
       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">
        rainforest
       </a>
       in lowlands. The Pacific coastal area has a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
        tropical climate
       </a>
       with a severe rainy season. The climate in the Andean highlands is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">
        temperate
       </a>
       and relatively dry, and the Amazon basin on the eastern side of the mountains shares the climate of other rainforest zones.
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of its location at the equator, Ecuador experiences little variation in daylight hours during the course of a year. Both sunrise and sunset occur each day at the two six o'clock hours.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">
        Hydrology
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rivers_of_Ecuador" title="Rivers of Ecuador">
        Rivers of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG/170px-Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG/255px-Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG/340px-Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_Pastazas_near_Banos.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_River" title="Pastaza River">
          Pastaza River
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Andes is the
       <i>
        watershed divisor
       </i>
       between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">
        Amazon
       </a>
       watershed, which runs to the east, and the Pacific, including the north–south rivers Mataje, Santiago,
       <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_River" title="Esmeraldas River">
        Esmeraldas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chone_River" title="Chone River">
        Chone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guayas_River" title="Guayas River">
        Guayas
       </a>
       , Jubones, and Puyango-Tumbes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Almost all of the rivers in Ecuador form in the La Sierra region and flow east toward the
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
        Amazon River
       </a>
       or west toward the Pacific Ocean. The rivers rise from snowmelt at the edges of the snowcapped peaks or from the abundant precipitation that falls at higher elevations. In the La Sierra region, the streams and rivers are narrow and flow rapidly over precipitous slopes. Rivers may slow and widen as they cross the hoyas yet become rapid again as they flow from the heights of the
       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
        Andes
       </a>
       to the lower elevations of the other regions. The highland rivers broaden as they enter the more level areas of the Costa and the Oriente.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Costa, the external coast has mostly intermittent rivers that are fed by constant rains from December through May and become empty riverbeds during the dry season. The few exceptions are the longer, perennial rivers that flow throughout the external coast from the internal coast and La Sierra on their way to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . The internal coast, by contrast, is crossed by perennial rivers that may flood during the rainy season, sometimes forming swamps.
      </p>
      <p>
       Major rivers in the Oriente include the
       <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_River" title="Pastaza River">
        Pastaza
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Napo_River" title="Napo River">
        Napo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Putumayo_River" title="Putumayo River">
        Putumayo
       </a>
       . The Pastaza is formed by the confluence of the Chambo and the Patate rivers, both of which rise in the Sierra. The Pastaza includes the Agoyan waterfall, which at sixty-one meters (200 feet) is the highest waterfall in Ecuador. The Napo rises near Mount Cotopaxi and is the major river used for transport in the eastern lowlands. The Napo ranges in width from 500 to 1,800 m (1,600 to 5,900 ft). In its upper reaches, the Napo flows rapidly until the confluence with one of its major tributaries, the Coca River, where it slows and levels off. The Putumayo forms part of the border with Colombia. All of these rivers flow into the
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
        Amazon River
       </a>
       . The Galápagos Islands have no significant rivers. Several of the larger islands, however, have freshwater springs although they are surrounded by the Pacific Ocean.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">
        Biodiversity
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_(crop).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2840" data-file-width="4088" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg/220px-A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg/330px-A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg/440px-A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_butterfly_feeding_on_the_tears_of_a_turtle_in_Ecuador_(crop).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Turtles and
         <i>
          Dryas iulia
         </i>
         , Ecuador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador is one of seventeen
       <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">
        megadiverse countries
       </a>
       in the world according to Conservation International,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservation_International_Site_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Conservation_International_Site-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and it has the most biodiversity per square kilometer of any nation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador has 1,600 bird species (15% of the world's known bird species) in the continental area and 38 more
       <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">
        endemic
       </a>
       in the Galápagos. In addition to over 16,000 species of plants, the country has 106 endemic reptiles, 138 endemic amphibians, and 6,000 species of butterfly. The Galápagos Islands are well known as a region of distinct fauna, famous as the place of birth of Darwin's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theory_of_Evolution" title="Theory of Evolution">
        Theory of Evolution
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       World Heritage Site.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador has the first constitution to recognize the rights of nature.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The protection of the nation's biodiversity is an explicit national priority as stated in the National Plan of "Buen Vivir", or good living, Objective 4, "Guarantee the rights of nature", Policy 1: "Sustainably conserve and manage the natural heritage, including its land and marine biodiversity, which is considered a strategic sector".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of the writing of the Plan in 2008, 19% of Ecuador's land area was in a protected area; however, the Plan also states that 32% of the land must be protected in order to truly preserve the nation's biodiversity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Current
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Ecuador" title="List of national parks in Ecuador">
        protected areas
       </a>
       include 11 national parks, 10 wildlife refuges, 9 ecological reserves, and other areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A program begun in 2008, Sociobosque, is preserving another 2.3% of total land area (6,295 km², or 629,500 ha) by paying private landowners or community landowners (such as Amerindian tribes) incentives to maintain their land as native ecosystems such as native forests or grasslands. Eligibility and subsidy rates for this program are determined based on the poverty in the region, the number of hectares that will be protected, and the type of ecosystem of the land to be protected, among other factors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite being on the UNESCO list, the Galápagos are endangered by a range of negative environmental effects, threatening the existence of this exotic
       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">
        ecosystem
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, oil exploitation of the Amazon rainforest has led to the release of billions of gallons of untreated wastes, gas, and crude oil into the environment, contaminating ecosystems and causing detrimental health effects to Amerindian peoples.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 985px;_width: 985px;">
       <li class="gallerycaption">
        Nature of the Galápagos Islands
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 189px">
        <div style="width: 189px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 184px;">
          <div style="margin:63.5px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg/154px-Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg/231px-Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg/308px-Galapagos_dominance_display.jpg 2x" width="154"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>

           </a>

        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 189px">
        <div style="width: 189px">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ecuador" title="Economy of Ecuador">
        Economy of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="932" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/220px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/330px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/440px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tree map of products exported by Ecuador in the HS4 product classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_economy" title="Developing economy">
        developing economy
       </a>
       that is highly dependent on commodities, namely petroleum and agricultural products. The country is classified as a medium-income country. Ecuador's economy is the eighth largest in Latin America and experienced an average growth of 4.6% between 2000 and 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From 2007 to 2012 Ecuador's GDP grew at an annual average of 4.3 percent, above the average for Latin America and the Caribbean, which was 3.5%, according to the United Nations' Economic Commission for Latin American and the Caribbean (ECLAC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ecuador was able to maintain relatively superior growth during the
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">
        crisis
       </a>
       . In January 2009 the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE) put the 2010 growth forecast at 6.88%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2011 its GDP grew at 8% and ranked 3rd highest in Latin America, behind Argentina (2nd) and Panama (1st).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Between 1999 and 2007, GDP doubled, reaching $65,490 million according to BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Inflation rate up to January 2008 was located about 1.14%, the highest recorded in the last year, according to the government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The monthly unemployment rate remained at about 6 and 8 percent from December 2007 until September 2008; however, it went up to about 9 percent in October and dropped again in November 2008 to 8 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Unemployment mean annual rate for 2009 in Ecuador was 8.5% because the global economic crisis continued to affect the Latin American economies. From this point unemployment rates started a downward trend: 7.6% in 2010, 6.0% in 2011, and 4.8% in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The extreme poverty rate has declined significantly between 1999 and 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2001 it was estimated at 40% of the population, while by 2011 the figure dropped to 17.4% of the total population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economy_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-economy-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is explained to an extent by emigration and the economic stability achieved after adopting the U.S. dollar as official means of transaction. However, starting in 2008 with the bad economic performance of the nations where most Ecuadorian emigrants work, the reduction of poverty has been realized through social spending mainly in education and health.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="917" data-file-width="1598" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg/220px-Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg/330px-Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg/440px-Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Industria_petrolera_ecuatoriana.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Refineries in Esmeraldas
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Oil accounts for 40% of exports and contributes to maintaining a positive trade balance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the late 1960s, the exploitation of oil increased production, and proven reserves are estimated at 6.51 billion barrels as of 2011
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The overall trade balance for August 2012 was a surplus of almost $390 million for the first six months of 2012, a huge figure compared with that of 2007, which reached only $5.7 million; the surplus had risen by about $425 million compared to 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economy_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-economy-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The oil trade balance positive had revenues of $3.295 million in 2008, while non-oil was negative, amounting to $2.842 million. The trade balance with the United States, Chile, the European Union, Bolivia, Peru, Brazil, and Mexico is positive. The trade balance with Argentina, Colombia, and Asia is negative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the agricultural sector, Ecuador is a major exporter of bananas (first place worldwide in production and export), flowers, and the seventh largest producer of cocoa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ecuador also produces coffee, rice, potatoes, cassava (manioc, tapioca), plantains and sugarcane; cattle, sheep, pigs, beef, pork and dairy products; fish, and shrimp; and balsa wood.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country's vast resources include large amounts of timber across the country, like eucalyptus and mangroves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Resources_Maps_World_Banks_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Resources_Maps_World_Banks-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pines and cedars are planted in the region of La Sierra and walnuts, rosemary, and balsa wood in the Guayas River Basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The industry is concentrated mainly in Guayaquil, the largest industrial center, and in Quito, where in recent years the industry has grown considerably. This city is also the largest business center of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Industrial production is directed primarily to the domestic market.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Despite this, there is limited export of products produced or processed industrially.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       These include canned foods, liquor, jewelry, furniture, and more.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       A minor industrial activity is also concentrated in Cuenca.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Industrias_en_Cuenca_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Industrias_en_Cuenca-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The incomes due to the tourism have been increasing during the last years because of the efforts of the Government of showing the variety of climates and the biodiversity in Ecuador.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2892" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/170px-Wtcgye.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/255px-Wtcgye.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/340px-Wtcgye.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         World Trade Center headquarters in
         <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
          Guayaquil
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador has negotiated bilateral treaties with other countries, besides belonging to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" title="Andean Community of Nations">
        Andean Community of Nations
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and an associate member of
       <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">
        Mercosur
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It also serves on the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       (WTO), in addition to the
       <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">
        Inter-American Development Bank
       </a>
       (IDB),
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       (IMF),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corporaci%C3%B3n_Andina_de_Fomento" title="Corporación Andina de Fomento">
        Corporación Andina de Fomento
       </a>
       (CAF) and other multilateral agencies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 2007, Ecuador paid off its debt to the IMF, thus ending an era of interventionism of the Agency in the country.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The public finance of Ecuador consists of the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE), the National Development Bank (BNF), the State Bank.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1738" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/220px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/330px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/440px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Quito" title="Trolleybuses in Quito">
          Trolebús
         </a>
         bus rapid transit system that runs through
         <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
          Quito
         </a>
         . It is the principal BRT in Ecuador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="588" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/220px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/330px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/440px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Railways in Ecuador
         <span class="nowrap">
          (
          <a class="extiw" href="//sharemap.org/public/Railways_in_Ecuador" title="sharemap:public/Railways in Ecuador">
           interactive map
          </a>
          )
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Ecuador" title="Transport in Ecuador">
        Transport in Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The rehabilitation and reopening of the Ecuadorian railroad and use of it as a tourist attraction is one of the recent developments in transportation matters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The roads of Ecuador in recent years have undergone important improvement. The major routes are Pan American (under enhancement from four to six lanes from Rumichaca to Ambato, the conclusion of 4 lanes on the entire stretch of Ambato and Riobamba and running via Riobamba to Loja). In the absence of the section between Loja and the border with Peru, there are the Route Espondilus and/or Ruta del Sol (oriented to travel along the Ecuadorian coastline) and the Amazon backbone (which crosses from north to south along the Ecuadorian Amazon, linking most and more major cities of it).
      </p>
      <p>
       Another major project is developing the road Manta – Tena, the highway Guayaquil – Salinas Highway Aloag Santo Domingo, Riobamba – Macas (which crosses Sangay National Park). Other new developments include the National Unity bridge complex in Guayaquil, the bridge over the Napo river in Francisco de Orellana, the Esmeraldas River Bridge in the city of the same name, and, perhaps the most remarkable of all, the Bahia – San Vincente Bridge, being the largest on the Latin American Pacific coast.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
        Mariscal Sucre International Airport
       </a>
       in Quito and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo_International_Airport" title="José Joaquín de Olmedo International Airport">
        José Joaquín de Olmedo International Airport
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       have experienced a high increase in demand and have required modernization. In the case of Guayaquil it involved a new air terminal, once considered the best in South America and the best in Latin America
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in Quito where an entire new airport has been built in Tababela and was inaugurated in February 2013, with Canadian assistance. However, the main road leading from Quito city centre to the new airport will only be finished in late 2014, making current travelling from the airport to downtown Quito as long as two hours during rush hour.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quito's old city-centre airport is being turned into parkland, with some light industrial use.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electrical_power_outlets">
        Electrical power outlets
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Electrical power outlets in Ecuador are the same as in the US (110v).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">
        Water supply and sanitation
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Ecuador" title="Water supply and sanitation in Ecuador">
        Water supply and sanitation in Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Drinking
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        water supply
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">
        sanitation
       </a>
       in Ecuador is characterized by a number of achievements and challenges. One key achievement is a significant increase in both access to an
       <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">
        improved water source
       </a>
       (82% in 1990 to 96% in 2010 in urban areas)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JMP-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">
        improved sanitation
       </a>
       (77% in 1990 to 96% in 2010 in urban areas). Significant increases in coverage in urban areas were achieved both by the public utility EMAAP-Q, serving the capital
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       , and the private concessionaire Interagua in the country's largest city
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       . However, municipalities rely overwhelmingly upon central government investment, rather than recouping the costs at a local level. Another problem is intermittent water supply, which affects half of the urban areas. Also, only 8% of all collected
       <a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">
        wastewater
       </a>
       is being treated. The level of
       <a href="/wiki/Non-revenue_water" title="Non-revenue water">
        non-revenue water
       </a>
       is estimated at 65%, one of the highest in Latin America.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Mobile_.28cellular.29_phone_frequencies">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_(cellular)_phone_frequencies">
        Mobile (cellular) phone frequencies
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Mobile (cellular) phone frequencies in Ecuador are 850 MHz, 1900 MHz, and 1700/2100 MHz (LTE).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_people" title="Ecuadorian people">
        Ecuadorian people
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:#ddd">
          <th colspan="5">
           Ethnic groups in Ecuador

            </a>
           </sup>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">

          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>

            White
           </a>
          </td>

           <div style="background:Green; width:6.1%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>

           6.1%
          </td>
         </tr>

           </a>

          </td>

           1.9%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Ecuadorians" title="Black Ecuadorians">
            Black
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:pink; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>

           1%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Other
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:gold; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           0.4%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador's population is ethnically diverse and the 2016 estimates put Ecuador's population at 16,385,068.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The largest ethnic group (as of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
         Mestizos
        </a>
       </i>
       , who are the descendants of Spanish colonists that interbred with Amerindian peoples, and constitute about 71% of the population. The White Ecuadorians (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">
        White Latin American
       </a>
       ) account for 6.1% of the population of Ecuador and can be found throughout all of Ecuador primarily around the urban areas. Even though Ecuador's white population during its colonial era were mainly descendants from Spain, today Ecuador's white population is a result of a mixture of European immigrants, predominantly from Spain with people from Italy, France, Germany, and Switzerland who have settled in the early 20th century. Ecuador also has people of middle eastern extraction that have also joined the ranks of the white minority. These include economically well off immigrants of Lebanese and Palestinian descent, who are either Christian or Muslim (
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">
        Islam in Ecuador
       </a>
       ). In addition, there is a small European Jewish (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Jews" title="Ecuadorian Jews">
        Ecuadorian Jews
       </a>
       ) population, which is based mainly in Quito and to a lesser extent in Guayaquil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethn_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethn-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_Peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous Peoples of the Americas">
        Amerindians
       </a>
       account for 7% of the current population. The mostly rural Montubio population of the coastal provinces of Ecuador, who might be classified as
       <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">
        Pardo
       </a>
       account for 7.4% of the population. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian_people" title="Afro-Ecuadorian people">
        Afro-Ecuadorians
       </a>
       is a minority population (7%) in Ecuador, that includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">
        Mulattos
       </a>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">
         zambos
        </a>
       </i>
       , and are largely based in the Esmeraldas province and to a lesser degree in the predominantly Mestizo provinces of Coastal Ecuador - Guayas and Manabi. In the Highland Andes where a predominantly Mestizo, white and Amerindian population exist, the African presence is almost non-existent except for a small community in the province of Imbabura called Chota Valley.
      </p>

           </a>

          </td>

           <div style="background:gold; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           0.4%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the Ecuadorian National Institute of Statistics and Census, 91.95% of the country's population have a religion, 7.94% are
       <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">
        atheists
       </a>
       and 0.11% are
       <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">
        agnostics
       </a>
       . Among the people that have a religion, 80.44% are Roman Catholic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_Rite" title="Latin Rite">
        Latin Rite
       </a>
       (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_in_Ecuador" title="List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador">
        List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador
       </a>
       ), 11.30% are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical" title="Evangelical">
        Evangelical
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestants
       </a>
       , 1.29% are
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       and 6.97% other (mainly Jewish, Buddhists and Latter-day Saints).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Francisco,_Quito_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3055" data-file-width="4583" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/220px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/330px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/440px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Francisco,_Quito_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Church of San Francisco
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the rural parts of Ecuador, Amerindian beliefs and Catholicism are sometimes
       <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">
        syncretized
       </a>
       . Most festivals and annual parades are based on religious celebrations, many incorporating a mixture of rites and icons.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a small number of
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
        Eastern Orthodox Christians
       </a>
       , Amerindian religions, Muslims (see
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">
        Islam in Ecuador
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">
        Buddhists
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" title="Bahá'í">
        Bahá'í
       </a>
       . According to their own estimates,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       accounts for about 1.4% of the population, or 211,165 members at the end of 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to their own sources, in 2012 there were 77,323
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first Jews arrived in Ecuador in the 16th and 17th centuries. Most of them are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic" title="Sephardic">
        Sephardic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">
        Anusim
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crypto-Jews" title="Crypto-Jews">
        Crypto-Jews
       </a>
       ) and many still speak
       <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">
        Judaeo-Spanish
       </a>
       (Ladino) language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Today the Jewish Community of Ecuador (Comunidad Judía del Ecuador) has its seat in
       <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">
        Quito
       </a>
       and has approximately 200 members. Nevertheless, this number is declining because young people leave the country for the United States or
       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
        Israel
       </a>
       . The Community has a Jewish Center with a
       <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">
        synagogue
       </a>
       , a country club, and a cemetery. It supports the "Albert Einstein School", where Jewish history, religion, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew" title="Hebrew">
        Hebrew
       </a>
       classes are offered. There are very small communities in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuenca_(Ecuador)" title="Cuenca (Ecuador)">
        Cuenca
       </a>
       . The "Comunidad de Culto Israelita" reunites the Jews of
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       . This community works independently from the "Jewish Community of Ecuador" and is composed of only 30 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nations">
        Nations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">
        Indigenous peoples in Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Ecuadorian constitution recognizes the "pluri-nationality" of those who want to exercise their affiliation with their native ethnic groups. Thus, in addition to
       <i>
        criollos
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        mestizos
       </i>
       , and Afro-Ecuadorians, some people belong to the Amerindian nations scattered in a few places in the coast, Quechua Andean villages, and the Amazonian jungle.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">
        Population genetics
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to a 2015
       <a href="/wiki/Genealogical_DNA_test" title="Genealogical DNA test">
        genealogical DNA testing
       </a>
       , the average Ecuadorian is estimated to be 52.96%
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">
        Native American
       </a>
       , 41.77%
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
        European
       </a>
       , and 5.26%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" title="Sub-Saharan African">
        Sub-Saharan African
       </a>
       overall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_density">
        Population density
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The majority of Ecuadorians live in the central provinces, the Andes mountains, or along the Pacific coast. The tropical forest region to the east of the mountains (El Oriente) remains sparsely populated and contains only about 3% of the population. Birth rate is 2-1 for each death. Marriages are usually from 14 and above using parental consent. About 12.4% of the population is married in the ages 15–19. Divorce rates are moderate.
       <br/>
       Population cities (2010)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo_de_2010_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-censo_de_2010-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration_and_emigration">
        Immigration and emigration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2012)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Ecuador" title="Emigration from Ecuador">
        Emigration from Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A small east
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Latino" title="Asian Latino">
        Asian Latino
       </a>
       community, estimated at 2,500, mainly consists of those of Japanese and Chinese descent, whose ancestors arrived as miners, farmhands and fishermen in the late 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early years of World War II, Ecuador still admitted a certain number of immigrants, and in 1939, when several South American countries refused to accept 165 Jewish refugees from Germany aboard the ship
       <i>
        Koenigstein
       </i>
       , Ecuador granted them entry permits.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years, Ecuador has grown in popularity among North American expatriates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They're drawn there by the authentic cultural experience and beautiful natural surroundings. Also, Ecuador's favorable residency options make for an easy transition for those who decide to settle there indefinitely.
      </p>
      <p>
       Another perk that draws many expats to Ecuador is its low cost of living. Since everything from gas to groceries costs far less than in North America, it's a popular choice for those who are looking to make the most of their retirement budget.
      </p>
      <p>
       Even real estate in Ecuador is much less than its tropical counterparts. However, as more and more North Americans are discovering Ecuador's potential, property prices are beginning to rise from where they were a decade ago, particularly in the areas that are popular among expats and tourists.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ecuador" title="Culture of Ecuador">
        Culture of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuadorian_dress,_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010,_London.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg/220px-Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg/330px-Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg/440px-Ecuadorian_dress%2C_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010%2C_London.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuadorian_dress,_Carnival_del_Pueblo_2010,_London.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A mestizo woman in Ecuadorian garment participating in the 2010
         <a href="/wiki/Carnaval_del_Pueblo" title="Carnaval del Pueblo">
          Carnaval del Pueblo
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ecuador's mainstream culture is defined by its Hispanic
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
         mestizo
        </a>
       </i>
       majority, and, like their ancestry, it is traditionally of Spanish heritage, influenced in different degrees by Amerindian traditions and in some cases by African elements. The first and most substantial wave of modern immigration to Ecuador consisted of Spanish colonists, following the arrival of Europeans in 1499. A lower number of other Europeans and North Americans migrated to the country in the late 19th and early twentieth centuries and, in smaller numbers, Poles, Lithuanians, English, Irish, and Croats during and after the Second World War.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG/220px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG/330px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG/440px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_001.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Alpaca" title="Alpaca">
          Alpaca
         </a>
         textile at the
         <a href="/wiki/Otavalo_(city)" title="Otavalo (city)">
          Otavalo
         </a>
         Artisan Market in the
         <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
          Andes
         </a>
         Mountains, Ecuador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG/220px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG/330px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG/440px-Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Otavalo_Artisan_Market_-_Andes_Mountains_-_South_America_-_photograph_007.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hand Painted Handcrafts at the Otavalo Artisan Market
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Since African slavery was not the workforce of the Spanish colonies in the Andes Mountains, given the subjugation of the Amerindian people through proselytization and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encomiendas" title="Encomiendas">
         encomiendas
        </a>
       </i>
       , the minority population of African descent is mostly found in the coastal northern province of Esmeraldas. This is largely owing to the 17th-century shipwreck of a slave-trading galleon off the northern coast of Ecuador. The few black African survivors swam to the shore and penetrated the then-thick jungle under the leadership of Anton, the chief of the group, where they remained as free men maintaining their original culture, not influenced by the typical elements found in other provinces of the coast or in the Andean region. A little later, runaway slaves from Colombia known as
       <i>
        cimarrones
       </i>
       joined them. In the small Chota Valley of the province of Imbabura exists a small community of Africans among the province's predominantly mestizo population. These blacks are descendants of Africans, who were brought over from Colombia by Jesuits to work their colonial sugar plantations as slaves. As a general rule, small elements of zambos and mulattoes coexisted among the overwhelming mestizo population of coastal Ecuador throughout its history as gold miners in Loja, Zaruma, and Zamora and as shipbuilders and plantation workers around the city of Guayaquil. Today you can find a small community of Africans in the Catamayo valley of the predominantly mestizo population of Loja.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ecuador's Amerindian communities are integrated into the mainstream culture to varying degrees,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but some may also practice their own native cultures, particularly the more remote Amerindian communities of the
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">
        Amazon basin
       </a>
       . Spanish is spoken as the first language by more than 90% of the population and as a first or second language by more than 98%. Part of Ecuador's population can speak
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">
        Amerindian
       </a>
       languages, in some cases as a second language. Two percent of the population speak only Amerindian languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Ecuador" title="Languages of Ecuador">
        Languages of Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:#ddd">
          <th colspan="5">
           Languages in Ecuador
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA_78-2">
            <a href="#cite_note-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA-78">
             [78]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
          <td style="padding:0 4px;">

          </td>

           </a>
           )
          </td>

          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>

          </td>

          </td>

         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Other Indigenous
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">

           </div>
          </td>
